## Domain Knowledge (LLM-generated)
**Domain**: nonlinear oscillator dynamics
**Analysis**: This is a nonlinear harmonic oscillator problem where acceleration (dv_dt) depends on position x through a nonlinear restoring force, velocity v through possible damping, and time t through possible external driving. The governing equation follows Newton's second law.

**Common formula structures in this domain**:
- Simple harmonic oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x (linear restoring force, no damping)
- Damped harmonic oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v (linear restoring force with linear damping)
- Driven damped oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v + c2 * sin(c3 * t) (with sinusoidal driving)
- Duffing oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 (cubic nonlinear restoring force)
- Damped Duffing oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * v (cubic nonlinearity with damping)
- Driven Duffing oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * v + c3 * cos(c4 * t) (full Duffing equation)
- Van der Pol oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * (1 - c2 * x**2) * v (nonlinear damping)
- Quintic nonlinearity: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * x**5 (higher-order restoring force)
- Softening spring: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x * Abs(x) (asymmetric nonlinear restoring force)
- Pendulum-like: dv_dt = c0 * sin(c1 * x) (sinusoidal restoring force approximating pendulum)
- Nonlinear damping: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v * Abs(v) (quadratic velocity damping)
- Parametric oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x * (1 + c1 * cos(c2 * t)) (time-modulated stiffness)
- Cubic damping with Duffing: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * v + c3 * v**3 (combined nonlinearities)
- Mathieu-Duffing: dv_dt = (c0 + c1 * cos(c2 * t)) * x + c3 * x**3 (parametric excitation with nonlinearity)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Odd-power restoring forces (x, x**3, x**5) preserve symmetry of oscillation about equilibrium — expect odd polynomial terms in x
- Nonlinear damping terms like (1 - x**2)*v indicate amplitude-dependent energy injection/dissipation (limit cycle behavior)
- Absence of explicit time dependence suggests an autonomous system (conservative or dissipative but undriven)
- If time appears, it likely enters through trigonometric functions sin(c*t) or cos(c*t) representing periodic driving forces
- Position-velocity coupling terms like x*v or x**2*v indicate nonlinear damping mechanisms where dissipation depends on displacement
- A pure function of x alone for dv_dt indicates a conservative system derivable from a potential energy function
- Sign of the leading x coefficient must be negative for bounded oscillatory motion (restoring force opposes displacement)
- Rational restoring forces like x/(1+c*x**2) model saturation of the restoring force at large amplitudes

2. A term `c*x*exp(-|x|)`: This is a very specific nonlinear function of x

4. `-sin(v)` term (note: `-β*sin(v)`)

The key challenge is matching the term `x*exp(-|x|)`. This is not a standard polynomial or simple power function. Let me check which candidates could potentially represent this.

Most candidates use polynomial terms, sin, cos, log, exp, power functions. The term `x*exp(-|x|)` is quite specific.

**Key observation:** None of the candidates contain `exp(-Abs(x))` or `x*exp(-|x|)` explicitly. So I need to check if any combination of terms in the candidates could reproduce this function for ALL x values.

The function `x*exp(-|x|)` behaves like:
- For small x: approximately `x - x²*sign(x) + ...` (not a simple polynomial)
- It's an odd function (since |x| is even, x*exp(-|x|) is odd)
- It decays to 0 as |x| → ∞

No finite polynomial can match `x*exp(-|x|)` for all x. No power function `x^c` can match it either (since x*exp(-|x|) decays while x^c either grows or goes to 0 differently). Log functions, sin functions of x, and exp(c*x) also cannot match this behavior for all x.

Let me check candidates with `exp(c*x)` terms (candidates 30, 46):
- **Candidate 30:** Has `c5*exp(c6*x)`. But `exp(c6*x)` is monotonic, while `x*exp(-|x|)` is not (and involves |x|). A single exponential can't match `x*exp(-|x|)` for all x.
- **Candidate 46:** Has `c5*exp(c6*x)` - same issue.

What about `log(c*x+1)` terms? These grow logarithmically, not decay, so they can't match `x*exp(-|x|)`.

Candidates with `sin(c*x)` (like 31, 35): `sin(c*x)` is periodic and bounded, can't match the non-periodic `x*exp(-|x|)`.

**Critical check on candidates 34, 40, 41, etc. with `x^c` terms:**
Setting `c6` to some value in `c5*x**c6` - no single power of x can match `x*exp(-|x|)` for all x.

After careful analysis, **none** of the candidates contain terms that can reproduce the `x*exp(-|x|)` behavior for all x. The available building blocks (polynomials, power functions, logarithms, exponentials of x, trigonometric functions of x) cannot combine to equal `x*exp(-|x|)` for all x values.

The term `x*exp(-|x|)` is a fundamentally different function that:
- Is non-analytic at x=0 (due to |x|)
- Decays exponentially for large |x|
- Cannot be represented by any finite combination of the available basis functions

No candidate can match the GT.
